<heading>

1.  CMMIRK-M34,1.3

ADVENT SONDAY.  CMMIRK-M34,1.4

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, +tys day, as +ge knowen well, ys cleped Sonenday
yn +te Aduent; +tat ys, +te Sonenday of Cristys comyng.  Wherfor +tys
day holy chyrch makyth mencyon of two comyngys of Crist, Godys sonne,
ynto +tys world, forto by mankind out of +te deueles bondage, and to
bryng hym and weldoers to +te blys +tat euer schall last.  CMMIRK-M34,1.6

And his o+ter comyng, +tat schall be at +te day of dome, forto deme all
wikytdoers ynto +te pyt of hell for euermor.  CMMIRK-M34,1.7

But +te $forme comyng of Cryst ynto +tys world broght ioy and blysse
wyth hym; CMMIRK-M34,1.8

+terfor holy chyrch vsyth summe songes of melody, as Alleluja and o+ter.
CMMIRK-M34,1.9

And for +te comyng of Cryst to +te dome schall be so jrus and so
cruell , +tat no tong may tell, +terfor holy chirch layth downe sum
songes of melody as:'Te Deum laudamus,''Gloria in excelsis,'and'
Weddyng. 'CMMIRK-M34,1.10

For aftyr +tat day schall weddyng neuer be.  CMMIRK-M34,1.11

+Tus holy chirche lay+te downe songys of melody befor, yn tokenyng of
vengans +tat woll come aftyr.  CMMIRK-M34,1.12

Then of +te fyrst comyng of Cryst into +tys world, +tus sayth Seynt
Austyne:'+Ter ben +tre +tyngys +tat ben ryuet yn +tys world: burth,
trauell, and de+te. 'CMMIRK-M34,1.13

+Tys ys +te testament +tat Adam, our formast fadyr, made to all his
ospryng aftyr hym, +tat ys: forto be borne yn sekenes, forto lyuen yn
trauayle, and forto dye yn drede.  CMMIRK-M34,1.14

But Crist - blessyt most he be!  - he come forto be executure of +tys
testament: CMMIRK-M34,1.15

and was borne, CMMIRK-M34,1.16

and trauayld, CMMIRK-M34,1.17

and dyet.  CMMIRK-M34,1.18

He was borne to bryng man out of sekenes ynto euerlastyng hele;
CMMIRK-M34,1.19

he trauaylde forto bryng man ynto euerlastyng <P_2> reste; CMMIRK-M34,2.20

he was ded forto bryng man ynto +te lyfe +tat neuer schall haue ende.
CMMIRK-M34,2.21

+Tys was +te cause of Crystys fyrst comyng ynto +tys world.  Wherfor he
+tat wyll scape +te dome +tat he wyll come to at +te second comyng, he
most lay downe all maner of pride and heynes of hert, and know hymselfe
+tat he ys not but a wryche and slyme of erth, and soo hold mekenes yn
his hert.  CMMIRK-M34,2.22

He most trauayl his body yn good werkes, and gete his lyfe wyth swynke,
and put away all ydylnes and slewth.  CMMIRK-M34,2.23

For he +tat wyll not trauayle here wyth men, as Seynt Barnard sayth,
he schall trauayle ay wyth +te fendes of hell.  CMMIRK-M34,2.24

And for dred of deth he mot make hym redy to his God, when he woll send
aftyr hym, +tat ys: schryuen of his synnys, and allway kepe his concyens
clene not forto abyde from lenton to lenton, but as sone as he fele+te
+tat he hath synnet, anoon goo schryue hym, and mekly take +te dome of
his schryft-fadyr: CMMIRK-M34,2.25

+ten schall he haue yn +te day of dome gret remedy and worschip.
CMMIRK-M34,2.26

For ryght as a knyght scheweth +te wondys +tat he ha+te yn batayle,
yn moche comendyng to hym; ryght so all +te synnys +tat a man hath
schryuen hym of, and taken hys penans for, schull be +ter yschewet yn
moch honowre to hym, and moche confucyon to +te fende.  CMMIRK-M34,2.27

And +tose +tat haue not schryuen hom, hit schall be schowet to all +te
world yn gret confusyon and schenschyp.  CMMIRK-M34,2.28

+Tys ys sayde for +te fyrst commyng of Cryst ynto +tys world.
CMMIRK-M34,2.29

The secunde comyng of hym to +te dome schall so cruell be, and ferdfull
, and horrybull, +tat +ter schal com befor xv dayes of gret drede;
CMMIRK-M34,2.30

so by +te drede of +tes dayes +tat comen befor, a man may know aparty the
horobylyte +tat schall be yn +te dome, +tat comyth aftyr.  CMMIRK-M34,2.31

The fyrst day, as Saynt Jerom sayth, +te see schall aryse vp yn hyr styd
, soo +tat +te watyr schall be hear then ayny hyll, by xl=ti= cubytys,
stondyng styll yn her styd, as hit wer a wall.  CMMIRK-M34,2.32

The ij. day hit schall fall downe, so +tat vnne+te hit schall
be yseyne.  CMMIRK-M34,2.33

The iij. day +te seeswyne and +te cloppys of +te see schull <P_3>
stond on +te see and make roryng noyse so hyddous, +tat no man can tell
hit but God hymselfe.  CMMIRK-M34,3.34

The iiij. day +te see and all watyrs schull bren.  CMMIRK-M34,3.35

The v. day treus and herbys schull swete blode, CMMIRK-M34,3.36

and all fowles schull come togedyr and no+ter ete ne drynke for ferd of
+te dome comyng.  CMMIRK-M34,3.37

The vj. day all byldyngys and castelles schull fall adowne to
+te grownde, CMMIRK-M34,3.38

and an horrybull fyre schall aryse at +te sonne goyng downe, and +ten
a+geyne at +te vprysyng of hym.  CMMIRK-M34,3.39

The vij. day all stons and rockes schull vche all tobeton o+ter
wyth a hydwes noyse, whech noyse God hymselfe schall know and vndyrstond.
CMMIRK-M34,3.40

The viij. day +te er+te schall quake so horribuly, +tat no best
schall stond on hit, CMMIRK-M34,3.41

but all schall fal to +te grownd.  CMMIRK-M34,3.42

The ix. day all hyllys and mowntaynys schull turne ynto powdyr,
CMMIRK-M34,3.43

and +te er+te schall be made playne and euen.  CMMIRK-M34,3.44

The x. day men schull goo out of hur dennys +ter +tay daret for
drede so amated for fer, +tat non schall speke to o+ter.  CMMIRK-M34,3.45

The xj. day all +te bones of +te ded men schull ryse and stond
vp on hor graues, CMMIRK-M34,3.46

and +tat day all graues schull opyn.  CMMIRK-M34,3.47

The xij. day sterres schull fall from heuen and spred out of hom
brennyng lemes.  CMMIRK-M34,3.48

The xiij. day all men schull be redy to aryse +tat haue ben
ded befor.  CMMIRK-M34,3.49

The xiiij. day heuen and er+te schull bren so horrybly, +tat no
man may tell hit.  CMMIRK-M34,3.50

The xv. day heuen and er+t schull be made newe, CMMIRK-M34,3.51

and all men and woymen and childyrne schull aryse vp yn +te age of xxx=ti=
+gere and come to +te dome.  CMMIRK-M34,3.52

Then schal Ihesu Crist, veray God and man, come to +te dome, and al
seyntys wyth hym, and schow all his wondys all fresch, and newe, and
bledyng, as +tat day +tat he deyet on +te crosse.  CMMIRK-M34,3.53

And +ter +te crosse schall be schewet all blody, and all o+ter
ynstrumentys of his passyon.  CMMIRK-M34,3.54

Then sory may +tay be +tat haue ben wont to swer by his hert, by sydes,
by blod and bones of hym; CMMIRK-M34,3.55

+tat schall be to hym a hygh fure and a hygh confusyon, CMMIRK-M34,3.56

but +tay wer sory +terof befor.  CMMIRK-M34,3.57

<P_4>

Then schall Cryst heghly +tonke hom, and prayse hom +tat han don mercy
to hor euen-cristyn, CMMIRK-M34,4.59

and schall say +tus to hom:'My fadyrs blessyd chyldyrne come+te ynto
+te joy +tat euer schall last.  CMMIRK-M34,4.60

For when I was hongry, +ge fedden me; CMMIRK-M34,4.61

when I was thursty, +ge gaf me dryngke; CMMIRK-M34,4.62

when I was naket, +ge clo+tet me; CMMIRK-M34,4.63

when I was herberles, +ge herbert me; CMMIRK-M34,4.64

when I was seke, +ge vyset me; +gevyng me +tat +tat was nedfull to me ;
CMMIRK-M34,4.65

when I was yn pryson, +ge come to me CMMIRK-M34,4.66

and confortet me.  CMMIRK-M34,4.67

For when +ge dyddyn +tus for my loue, +ge dydden hyt to me CMMIRK-M34,4.68

and as moche +tonke I kan you for +tat +ge dydden to +te lest of myn,
as +ge hadden don hit to myn owne selfe; wherfor goo +ge now ynto +tat
ioye +tat euer schall last. 'CMMIRK-M34,4.69

Then schall he horrubly rebuken ryche men +tat han don no mercy, and say
to hom spytwysly +tus:'Goo +ge curset lystes ynto +te payne of helle,
CMMIRK-M34,4.70

for +ge hadden ynogh wherof to haue fed me and my seruantys, and +geue
me dryngke, yclo+tet me, and herbert me, and holpen me yn my sekenes,
and vyset me yn my dyses, CMMIRK-M34,4.71

and +ge wold not, CMMIRK-M34,4.72

but louet your good and not me.  Wherfor goo +ge now ynto +te fyre
of helle +tat ys ordeynt to +te fendys of hell wythout any mercy;
CMMIRK-M34,4.73

for +ge wold do no mercy, CMMIRK-M34,4.74

and +terfor +ge schull haue no mercy. 'CMMIRK-M34,4.75

Then woo schall be to hom +tat schall here +tys rebuke yn +tat day;
CMMIRK-M34,4.76

+ter schall no pleder helpe, ne gold, ne syluyr, ne othyr yftes;
CMMIRK-M34,4.77

but as a man hath don, he schall haue.  CMMIRK-M34,4.78

He schall haue accusars aboue hym, wythyn hym, on aythyr syde hym,
and vndyr hym, +tat he schall no way scape.  CMMIRK-M34,4.79

Aboue hym schall be Crist his domes-man so wro+te, +tat no tong con tell
, for he dyt no mercy; wythyn hym his on concyens accusyng hym of +te
lest +toght +tat euer he dyd amys; hys angyll on +tat on syde tellyng
hym redely wher and how oft he ha+te don amys; on +tat o+ter syde fendes
chalenchyng hym horres as by ryght; vndyr hym helle +geonyng, and galpyng,
and spyttyng fyre and stench forto swolon hym ynto +te payne +tat neuer
schall haue ende.  CMMIRK-M34,4.80

Thys, good men, +ge schull know well +tat yn +te day of dome pore men
schull be domes-men wyth Cryst, and dome +te ryche.  CMMIRK-M34,4.81

For all +te woo +tat pore men hauen, hit ys by +te ryche men;
CMMIRK-M34,4.82

<P_5>

and +togh +tay haue moche wrong, +tay may not gete amendes, tyll +tay
come to +tat dome; CMMIRK-M34,5.84

and +ter +tay schall haue all hor one lust of hom.  CMMIRK-M34,5.85

For when +tay haue wrong, and mow gete non amendys, +ten +tay pray ful
hertely to God forto qwyt hom yn +te day of dome; CMMIRK-M34,5.86

and woll he truly.  CMMIRK-M34,5.87

For +tus he sayth by his profyt:'Kepytt your veniauns to me, and I wyll
qwyt you. 'Wherfor, syrs, for Goddys loue, whyll +ge byn here, makyth
amendes for your mys-dedys, and maky+te hom your frendes +tat schall
be our domes-men, and tryst +ge not to hom +tat schall com aftyr you,
lest +ge ben deseyuet, and dredyth +te payne of hell +tat schall last
wythouten any ende.  CMMIRK-M34,5.88

Seynt Bede telle+te +tat +ter was a husbond-man here yn Englond
+tat fell seke, and lay as for ded from +te euentyde tyll +te morow.
CMMIRK-M34,5.89

+Ten aros he, CMMIRK-M34,5.90

and departed his gedys yn +tre partyes, CMMIRK-M34,5.91

and his partye he gaf to pore men, CMMIRK-M34,5.92

and +gede CMMIRK-M34,5.93

and was made a monke yn an abbay +tat stod by a watyr syde.  Ynto +te
whech watyr ych nyght he +gede yn, wer hyt neuer soo coold forste,
CMMIRK-M34,5.94

and stod ther long tyme of +te nyght.  CMMIRK-M34,5.95

And when he was asket, why he put hymselfe ynto so moche penaunce , he
vnswered:'Forto eschoyn +te more payne +tat I haue seyn, 'CMMIRK-M34,5.96

and ete barly-bred, CMMIRK-M34,5.97

and dranke watyr all his lyfe aftyr.  CMMIRK-M34,5.98

And he wold tell to relygyous men +te payne +tat he segh, +tat was soo
gret, +tat he cowthe not tel hit openly.  CMMIRK-M34,5.99

He sayde +tat an angyll lad hym ynto a place +tat on +te toon syde was
suche a colde, that no tong myght tell +te payne +terof; CMMIRK-M34,5.100

and on +tat o+ter syde was suche a hete, +tat no man myght tell +te
payne +terof, ny of +te hete: CMMIRK-M34,5.101

and sowles wern cast out of +tat won into +te to+ter.  CMMIRK-M34,5.102

And so +tat angyll schewet hym +te fyre +tat come out at +te mow+te,
+tat was +te fyre of hell; +tat was so hote, +tat als ferre as he myght
seen hit, hym +toght he brennet for hete.  CMMIRK-M34,5.103

And yn +te lees +terof he segh sowles bulmyng vp and don, cryyng
horrybuly, and a noyse of fendes cryyng:'Sle, sle, sle, sle, sle, sle,
CMMIRK-M34,5.104

opon +te broche, CMMIRK-M34,5.105

rost hote, CMMIRK-M34,5.106

cast ynto +te cawdren, CMMIRK-M34,5.107

sethe fast yn pyche, and cood, and brymston, and hot leed! '
CMMIRK-M34,5.108

+Tus +tay +tat ben dampnet to hell, +tay styntyn neuer to cry and +gelle
:'Woo ys hym +tat +tedyr schall goo. 'CMMIRK-M34,5.109

God hymselfe scheld vs +terfro, CMMIRK-M34,5.110

and bryng vs to +te blys he boght vs to.  CMMIRK-M34,5.111

Amen.  CMMIRK-M34,5.112

<heading>

2.  CMMIRK-M34,6.115

DE FESTO SANCTI ANDREE ET EIUS SOLEMPNITATE SERMO BREUIS.
CMMIRK-M34,6.116

<$$heading>

Good men and weymen, such a day +ge schull haue Seynt Andrawys daye,
and fast +te euen.  +Te whech dey +ge schull come to +te chyrch to serue
God, and forto worschip the holy apostoll for +te speciall uertues +tat
he hade: CMMIRK-M34,6.118

an for his hygh holynes of lyvyng, ano+ter for gret myracles doyng,
the thrid for gret pas-syon suffryng.  CMMIRK-M34,6.119

He was a man of holy lyuing; CMMIRK-M34,6.120

for when he herd +tat Seynt Ion Baptyst prechet yn deserte, he $laft al
his worldes occupacyon, CMMIRK-M34,6.121

and +gede to hym, CMMIRK-M34,6.122

and was his descypull.  CMMIRK-M34,6.123

Then befell hit apon a day Crist come walkyng, CMMIRK-M34,6.124

and when Seynt Ion segh hym walkyng, he sayde +tys to his dyscypull:
CMMIRK-M34,6.125

'Lo, +gonde ys Godys lombe +tat schall do away +te syn of +te world.
'CMMIRK-M34,6.126

And when Seynt Andrew herd +tat, anon he laft Ion CMMIRK-M34,6.127

and suet Cryst.  CMMIRK-M34,6.128

And when he herd Crist preche, hym lyket soo well +tat he fatte Seynt
Petyr, his bro+ter, to Crist forto here his prechyng.  CMMIRK-M34,6.129

And +ten +tay bo+te casten such a loue to Cryst, +tat on a day sone
aftyr, as +tay wer yn +te see of Galyle fyschyng, Cryst come by hom,
and callet hom.  CMMIRK-M34,6.130

+Ten +tay bo+te anon laften hor schippe, and hor nettys, and all +tat
+tay hadden, CMMIRK-M34,6.131

and sewet Crist for+te ay, tyll he stegh ynto Heuen.  CMMIRK-M34,6.132

And when he was gon ynto Heuen, Andraw prechet Goddys worde to +te pepull.
Among +te wheche was on, callad Nicol, +tat lyvet lx=ti= wyntyr and more
yn lechery.  CMMIRK-M34,6.133

But by grace of God he +toght to amende his lyfe, CMMIRK-M34,6.134

and let wryte a gospell on a boke, CMMIRK-M34,6.135

and had +tat wyth hym yn hopyng +tat +te vertu of Cryst schull put away
his temptacyon.  CMMIRK-M34,6.136

And soo, by +te vertu of Goddys worde, he abstaynet hym of his synne a
while; CMMIRK-M34,6.137

but +get by entysyng of +te fend, on a day, he for+get hymselfe,
CMMIRK-M34,6.138

and +gede to +te bordell-hous, as he was wont to do.  CMMIRK-M34,6.139

And when he come +tedyr, +te womon criet vpon hym, CMMIRK-M34,6.140

and sayde:'Vnsley old man, goo he+ten!  CMMIRK-M34,6.141

for I se apon +te mony meruayles. 'CMMIRK-M34,6.142

+Ten +tys Nycol by+toght hym +tat he hade Goddys gospell on hym.
CMMIRK-M34,6.143

And anon he +gede to Seynt Andraw, CMMIRK-M34,6.144

and told hym +tys caas, CMMIRK-M34,6.145

and prayde hym forto pray for hym to God +tat his sole wer not forlorne.
CMMIRK-M34,6.146

Then Seynt Andraw sayde +tat he wold neuer ete ne <P_7> dryng, tyll he
wyst whe+ter he schuld be saued or noo.  CMMIRK-M34,7.147

+Ten he fast fyf dayees prayng and bysechyng for hym.  CMMIRK-M34,7.148

+Ten, at +te fyuet dayes ende, +ter come a voyce to hym, CMMIRK-M34,7.149

and sayde:'As +tou fastes and prayes to God, make Nycol forto don;
and +ten he schall be sauet. 'CMMIRK-M34,7.150

+Ten callet he +tis Nicol to hym, CMMIRK-M34,7.151

and bade hym fast fourty dayes bred and watyr, and pray bysily to God ;
CMMIRK-M34,7.152

and soo he dyd.  CMMIRK-M34,7.153

And when +te fourty dayes wer done, sone aftyr +tys Nicol deyd.
CMMIRK-M34,7.154

+Ten come +ter a voyce to Andraw, CMMIRK-M34,7.155

and sayde:'By +ty prayer I haue wonen Nicoll +tat was lost.
'CMMIRK-M34,7.156

<heading>

Narracio.  CMMIRK-M34,7.158

<$$heading>

Also a +gong man com to Seynt Andraw, CMMIRK-M34,7.160

and preuely sayde to hym:'Syr, my modyr ha+te besoght me forto lye by
hure; CMMIRK-M34,7.161

but for I wold not, hoo hath accuset me to +te justyce.  Wherfor well
I wot y schall be ded.  CMMIRK-M34,7.162

And +get I haue leuer take +te deth +ten sclaundyr my modyr soo fowle.
Wherfor, syr, for Godys loue pray for me +tat I may take my deth
mekely. 'CMMIRK-M34,7.163

+Ten sayde Saynt Andraw:'Sonne, goo forth to +ty dome, and I wyll goo
wyth +te. 'CMMIRK-M34,7.164

+Ten anon comme men, CMMIRK-M34,7.165

and fatten hym to +te justyce.  CMMIRK-M34,7.166

And his modyr accusyt hym styfly to +te justice; CMMIRK-M34,7.167

and he held his tong, CMMIRK-M34,7.168

and sayd naght.  CMMIRK-M34,7.169

Then spake Seynt Andraw CMMIRK-M34,7.170

and sayde to hys modyr:'+Tou wyket woman, +tat for lust of +ti lechery
art aboute to do +ti sonne to deth; veniaunce wol fall apon the!
'CMMIRK-M34,7.171

+Ten seyd ho to +te justyce:'Syr, sy+ten my sonne wold haue done
+tys orybull dede, and myght not spede, he has drawen to +tys man for
socowr. 'CMMIRK-M34,7.172

+Ten +te justyce commaundet to put +te sonne yn a fet, and cast hym yn
a watyr forto drowne hym, and Andraw ynto prison, tyll he wer aviset on
what de+te {on} he schuld sle hym.  CMMIRK-M34,7.173

Then Saynt Andraw $prayde bysyly to God for help.  CMMIRK-M34,7.174

+Ten anon com a hydewes +tondyr +tat made all hom aferde, +tat +tay wern
all fayne to fach Andraw out of pryson.  CMMIRK-M34,7.175

And +terwyth com a bolt of layte, CMMIRK-M34,7.176

and brant +te modyr to colys yn syght of all men.  CMMIRK-M34,7.177

And +tus he sauet +te man fro +te deth, CMMIRK-M34,7.178

and turnet +te justyce and all +te pepull to +te faythe of Crist.
CMMIRK-M34,7.179

Herby +ge may vndyrstond +tat he was a man of holy lyvyng.
CMMIRK-M34,7.180

He was also gret yn myracles doyng.  CMMIRK-M34,7.181

For on a day, as he walket on +te see-warth, he segh a drownet man cast
vp on +te <P_8> watyr.  CMMIRK-M34,8.182

+Ten he prayde to God to reysen hym to lyue.  CMMIRK-M34,8.183

+Ten anon +tys body ros to lyue.  CMMIRK-M34,8.184

And when he was raysed to lyue, Seynt Andraw askyt hym how he was drownet.
CMMIRK-M34,8.185

+Ten he vnsward CMMIRK-M34,8.186

and sayd +tus:'We wer fourty +geong men ynfere, CMMIRK-M34,8.187

and herden of a holy man +tat was yn +tys contre, CMMIRK-M34,8.188

and wolden haue gon to hym to haue herd his prechyng.  CMMIRK-M34,8.189

But when we wern yn +te see, a tempest comme on vs, CMMIRK-M34,8.190

and drownet all ynfere.  CMMIRK-M34,8.191

But wold God +tat we haden ben cast vp all ynfere, +tat we myghten haue

3.  CMMIRK-M34,11.303

Goode men and woymen, such a day ys Saynt Nycholas-daye.  +Te wheche
nome ys vndyrstonden +te praysyng of +te pepull; CMMIRK-M34,11.306

That ys +te joy +tat lestyth ay.  CMMIRK-M34,21.596

Amen.  CMMIRK-M34,21.597

Ion Grysostom seyth, +tat Thomas come to +tat contray wher +te
kynges of Coleyne were, and folowed hom, and made hom crysten men.
CMMIRK-M34,21.598

For, +togh +tay haden worschypped Crist yn his burthe, +tay herden
no more of hym, tyll Thomas come to home, and taght hom +te faythe.
+Te whyche now +tay lyne at Colen.  CMMIRK-M34,21.599

<heading>

6.  CMMIRK-M34,21.601

DE NATIVITATE DOMINI NOSTRI IHESU CRSTI ET EIUS SOLEMPNITATE.
CMMIRK-M34,21.602

<$$heading>

Godde men and woymen and crysten creatures, as +ge here and sethe,
+tys day all holy chyrche syngythe, and redythe, and maketh melody yn
mynde of +te swete byr+te of our Lord, Ihesu Cryst, veray God and man,
+tat was as +tys day borne of hys modyr, Seynt Mary, yn gret help and
socour to all monkynd, but specyaly for +tre causes: forto +gyue pes to

Then, as to +te forme cause +tat he was borne forto +geuen pes to men

For when he was borne angeles songen +tus:'Gloria in excelsis Deo. '+Tat

At $mydnyght Crist was borne, CMMIRK-M34,21.608

for +ten alle +tyng be kynd taketh rest yn schewyng +tat he ys prynce
of pes, and was comen to make pes bytwyx God and man, and bytwyx angeles
and man, and bytwyx man and man.  CMMIRK-M34,21.609

He made pes bytwyx God and mon; wherfore forto be a trewe mediatur bytwyx
hom, he toke kynde of bo+te: and veray God and man.  CMMIRK-M34,21.610

And soo, by hys medyacyon, he knet +te loue of God to man so sadly,
+tat +te fadyr of Heuen spared not his owne sonne, but send hym forto
bye man wyth his blod, and bryng hym by wayes of mekenes a+geyne to +te
joye of paradyse +tat man lost by couetyse and heghnes.  CMMIRK-M34,21.611

Thus he made pes bytwyx God and man.  CMMIRK-M34,21.612

He made pes bytwyx angeles and man; CMMIRK-M34,21.613

vnbuxamnes - fore vmbuxomnes is a thing that angeles haten - wherfor

+tay deden mon worschippe, CMMIRK-M34,22.614

Thus he made pes bytwyx angeles and man.  CMMIRK-M34,22.619

For a+geyne tyme +tat he wold be borne, he made such pes +trogh all +te

+Tus, good men, +ge mou vndyrstonde how God +geueth pes to hom

Herby, good men, +ge schull vndyrstond +tat Cryst heled not +too +tat

Yn tokenyng of +tis +te secunde masse of this day ys sayde yn +te dawyng

'Lyght schall <P_25> schyne +tys day apon vs. 'CMMIRK-M34,25.686

+Tus Crystys burth lyghtned mony +tat befor loket euell.

<heading>

7.  CMMIRK-M34,26.728

DE FESTO SANCTI STEPHANI ET EIUS SOLEMPNITATE.  CMMIRK-M34,26.729

<$$heading>

Blessyd pepyll of Goddys mowth, +tat byn comen +tys day to holy chyrche
yn worschyp of God and +tys holy martyr, Seynt Steven, +tat ys callet
Goddys fyrst martyr, for +te enchesen +tat he was +te fyrst martyr +tat
sufferd deth for Crystys loue, aftyr +tat he was ascendet ynto Heuen.
CMMIRK-M34,26.731

Then, forto ster you to deuocyon +te more to +tis holy martyr, +ge schull
now here what he sufferd <P_27> for Crystys loue.  CMMIRK-M34,27.732

As +te boke of +te dedys of +te apostoles tellyth, whan Cryst was styet
vp into Heuen, +te apostoles tentedon all to prechyng of Goddys wordes
and to holy prayeours, CMMIRK-M34,27.733

and myght not serue all +tat turneden to +te fayth, CMMIRK-M34,27.734

+tay chosen syx holy men and goode out of syxty and ten +tat wern Crystys
dyscyples forto helpen hom yn Goddys seruyce.  Of +te wheche Seynt
Steven was +te fyrst and +te wysyst, and was full of grace and myght
of +te Holy Gost, +tat he dyd mony wondres and myracles yn +te pepyll.
CMMIRK-M34,27.735

But, +tagh a man be neuer soo holy a lyuer, +get he schall haue enmyes.
Wherfor +te Iewes of dyuerse contre +tat haden envy to Seynt Steuen,
rysen, a+geynes hym, and dysputed wyth hym a+geynes Crystys faythe,
hauyng full purpos, yf +tay myghten, to ouercome hym by dysputson,
and by fals wytnes, to do hym to deth.  CMMIRK-M34,27.736

But when Seynt Steven knew hor males, he +toght forto sese hom wyth won of
+tes +tre wayes: by schamyng yn dysputeson, o+tir by drede of reuelacyon,
othyr by loue and holy oryson.  CMMIRK-M34,27.737

But furst he assayeth by schamyng and dysputeson.  CMMIRK-M34,27.738

For +tay began to dyspute wyth hym; CMMIRK-M34,27.739

but he was so full of +te Holy Gost, +tat +tay haden no wytte ne no
powste forto +geynestonde hym.  CMMIRK-M34,27.740

But openly he ouercome yn all hor maters, CMMIRK-M34,27.741

and preued hor wyttys fals, CMMIRK-M34,27.742

and sayde, he was redy forto take dethe yn verefyyng of all +tat he
had sayde.  CMMIRK-M34,27.743

CMMIRK-M34,27.744

But algate a+geynstode +te Holy Gost +tat spake yn hor hertes,
CMMIRK-M34,27.745

and schewet hom yn concyens +tat +tay dedden amys.  CMMIRK-M34,27.746

And, $+ter $as {TEXT:+teras} +tay seen +te comyn pepull turne to +te

algate a+geynestoden styfly, CMMIRK-M34,27.747

+Ten wer +tay more anangrede a+geynes hym, CMMIRK-M34,27.749

and freton hor hertys wythyn, CMMIRK-M34,27.750

and gryspude wyth hor teeth a+geynes hym.  CMMIRK-M34,27.751

And, for +tay myght not ouercome hym wyth dyspytson, +tay +toghten forto

and lyft vp his een ynto Heuen CMMIRK-M34,28.754

CMMIRK-M34,28.755

'Chyldren, loue+t yche on othyr. 'CMMIRK-M34,34.966

+Ten sayde on to hym:'Fadyr, why say +ge +tus soo oft? ' CMMIRK-M34,34.967

+Ten sayde he:'For, yf +ge louen togedyr, hit ys jnogh to saluacyon.
'CMMIRK-M34,34.968

Then made he to make hym a graue before +te auter.  CMMIRK-M34,34.969

And when hyt was made, he lay downe yn hit; CMMIRK-M34,34.970

and ther come such a lyght apon hym, a gret whyll, +tat no man myght
see hym.  CMMIRK-M34,34.971

And when +tis lyght was gon, +te put was full of manna, CMMIRK-M34,34.972

and wallut vp so doth sonde yn well wyth watyr.  CMMIRK-M34,34.973

In +te lyfe of Saynt Edward +te Confessour +tat lythe at Westmynster,
ys wrytten +tat Saynt Ion aperyth to Seynt Edward on a day, as he +gode
on processyon, CMMIRK-M34,34.974

and prayd hym forto +geue hym summe good for Seynt Ionys loue,
th'Evangelyst; CMMIRK-M34,34.975

for he louet hym moche.  CMMIRK-M34,34.976

But for +te kyng hadde noght elles redy forto +geue hym, he toke +te
ryng of hys fyngyr, CMMIRK-M34,34.977

and +gaf hym; CMMIRK-M34,34.978

and soo Ion had +te ryng VII +gere.  CMMIRK-M34,34.979

And at +te VII +gerys ende, Ion aperet to a knyght of +te kyngys by+gonde
+te see, CMMIRK-M34,34.980

and bade hym bere +tat ryng to +te kyng, CMMIRK-M34,34.981

and bade hym be+tenke hym well for whos sake he +gaf hyt away, and say
+tat he greteth hym wele, CMMIRK-M34,34.982

and bade hym make hym redy, CMMIRK-M34,34.983

for he schall dey sone.  CMMIRK-M34,34.984

And so he dyd, CMMIRK-M34,34.985

and +gede to +te blysse of Heuen.  To +te whech blysse God bryng you
and me to, yf hit be his wyll.  CMMIRK-M34,34.986

Amen.  CMMIRK-M34,34.987

<heading>

9.  CMMIRK-M34,35.990

DE INNOCENTIBUS ET EORUM FESTIUITATE.  CMMIRK-M34,35.991

<$$heading>

Goddys owne blessed chyldern, +tat byn comen +tis day to holy chyrch yn
+te worschyp of God and +te chyldern +tat weren yslayne for Goddys sake.
CMMIRK-M34,35.993

As holy chyrche +tis day maketh mynde, and redu+te and syngythe of hom,
+tes chyldren ben called yn holy chyrche Innocentys, +tat ys yn Englysche
: wytheouten nye.  CMMIRK-M34,35.994

For +tay wer not nyes to God by pride, CMMIRK-M34,35.995

for God ys euer anyed wyth pryde, men and woymen, CMMIRK-M34,35.996

and a+gaynestondyth hom, nor to hor neghtbur by no wrong doyng, ny to
homselfe by no concent of synne.  CMMIRK-M34,35.997

I may well say, +tay lyueden here clanly wythout schame, +tay dyedyn
wythout blame, and wern folowed yn her same.  CMMIRK-M34,35.998

This Innocentes +tat holy chyrche syngeth of, lyueden her wythout schame
; CMMIRK-M34,35.999

for +tay wer all within two +ger of age.  Wherfor +tay wer not aschamet
of hor owne schappe; CMMIRK-M34,35.1000

for when a chyld ys wythyn state of innocentes, he ys not aschamet of
hys schappe, CMMIRK-M34,35.1001

for he ys not defowled wyth fulth of synne, CMMIRK-M34,35.1002

but of +te synne +tat he hathe, he draweth of +te synne of Adam and
of Eue.  CMMIRK-M34,35.1003

For so ferden +tey yn +te same wyse.  CMMIRK-M34,35.1004

For whyle +tay wer yn paradyse yn +te state of jnnocentes, +tay wer
naket; CMMIRK-M34,35.1005

but +tay wer not aschamet of hor schappe, CMMIRK-M34,35.1006

for +tay wer wythout synne.  CMMIRK-M34,35.1007

But as sone as +tay haden synned, +tay seen hor schappe,
CMMIRK-M34,35.1008

and wern aschamet +terof, CMMIRK-M34,35.1009

and hydden hit wyth leues of fygge-tre.  CMMIRK-M34,35.1010

Thus, when synne bygynnyth to take rote yn a chyld, +ten jnnocentes
gothe away; CMMIRK-M34,35.1011

for +ten he begynnyth to know +te good from +te euell.  CMMIRK-M34,35.1012

+Ten he synneth, CMMIRK-M34,35.1013

and +ten he greueth hys God.  CMMIRK-M34,35.1014

But +tes chyldyr lyued not soo long forto knew +te good from +te euell,
CMMIRK-M34,35.1015

but wern jslayne wythyn degre of jnnocentes.  Wherfor +tay lyuedon here
wythout schame.  CMMIRK-M34,35.1016

+Tay dyeden alsoo wythout blame; CMMIRK-M34,35.1017

for Herode, kyng of Iewes, made to sle hom wythout gult.
CMMIRK-M34,35.1018

For when +te kyngys comen to Herod, and askyt hym wher +te kyng of
Iewes was borne, and bede tell hom, for +tay wern comen to worschyppe
hym ferr out of +te est.  +Ten was Herod all astonyed of hor wordes,
CMMIRK-M34,35.1019

and asked his clerkes wher he schuld be borne.  CMMIRK-M34,35.1020

+Ten sayde +tay yn +te cyte <P_36> of Bedeleem.  CMMIRK-M34,36.1021

+Ten sayde Herod to +te kynges, byddyng hom goo +tedyr, and do hym
worschip; and come a+geyne to hym, and telle hym all hor doyng, +tat he
myght come and worschip hym also.  CMMIRK-M34,36.1022

But when +tes kynges haden don hor offryng to Cryst, +tay +gedyn hom by
anothyr way.  CMMIRK-M34,36.1023

Then was Horod wondyr wrothe, CMMIRK-M34,36.1024

and schaped anon to haue slayn Cryst.  CMMIRK-M34,36.1025

But when he had made hym redy +terfor, +tat same tyme, +te Emperour of
Rome sende to hym by lettyr forto come to hym yn all +te hast +tat {in}
he myght; CMMIRK-M34,36.1026

for two of his owne sonnes hadden apechet hym of traytery to +te Emperour.
CMMIRK-M34,36.1027

Soo at +tat tyme he laft +te sleyng of Cryst, CMMIRK-M34,36.1028

and +gede to Rome, CMMIRK-M34,36.1029

and had +te bettyr of hys sonnes, CMMIRK-M34,36.1030

Then send he anon men, CMMIRK-M34,36.1032

and bade sle all +te chyldyr +tat weren yn Bedeleem and yn +te contrey
abowte, +tat wer too +ger old and wythynn, +tagh hyt were a chyld +tat
was borne +tat same day.  CMMIRK-M34,36.1033

And soo +tay dedyn.  CMMIRK-M34,36.1034

He was aferd, lest Crist +tat made +te sterre brynge +te kynges so ferre
, cou+te haue turnet hym ynto dyuerse ages, and made hymselfe oldyr or
+gongyr, at his one lyst.  CMMIRK-M34,36.1035

And for he was a +gere goyng and comyng to Rome, +terfor he made to sle

And for wrach schuld falle on hymselfe yn party, +terfor a chyld of

CMMIRK-M34,36.1037

But +ten come +ter an angyll to Ioseph, CMMIRK-M34,36.1038

And so +tay dyden.  CMMIRK-M34,36.1040

+Tus +tes Innocentes wern slayn wythout blame.  CMMIRK-M34,36.1041

Thay wer also folowed yn hor same, +tat ys to say, yn hor owne blod.
CMMIRK-M34,36.1042

+Tay wer not folowet yn no font, but yn $schedyng of hor blod.  Wherfor
+ge schull vndrystond +tat folo+gt come+t +tre maner of wyse: yn watyr,

+tay wern folowed yn fologht of faythe.  CMMIRK-M34,36.1045

Thus +ge mou see how much cruelte +tis man <P_37> had yn hert, +tat

+Ten, for he made mony a modyr chyldles, and forto wepe for hor

CMMIRK-M34,37.1047

And aftyr, as he pared an appull, wyth +te same knyfe he slogh hymselfe.
CMMIRK-M34,37.1048

Thus he +tat was lusty for to schedde gyltles blod, at +te last he
schedde hys owne hert-blod.  CMMIRK-M34,37.1049

For he that ys wythout mercy, vengeans schall fall apon hym.
CMMIRK-M34,37.1050

And he +tat loueth to do mercy, God wyll +geue hym mercy.
CMMIRK-M34,37.1051

And +tis I aferme by ensampull +tat I fynde yn +te lyfe of Seynt
Syluestyr.  CMMIRK-M34,37.1052

Ther I fynde +tat Constantyn, +te Emperour, was mesele and, by consele
of hys leches, he made forto get +tre +towsand chyldren yfere, forto
haue slayn hom; CMMIRK-M34,37.1053

and all hor blod schuld haue be done yn a vessell, and +te Emperour be
bathyd +teryn, whyll hit had ben hote.  CMMIRK-M34,37.1054

Then when +tese chyldren wern gedert yn a place, +tis Emperour com rydyng
in a chare +tedyr.  CMMIRK-M34,37.1055

+Ten asket +te Emperour, what woymen +tay wern.  CMMIRK-M34,37.1057

+Ten sayden o+ter, +tay wern +te modyrs of +te chyldren +tat schuld be

CMMIRK-M34,37.1059

+Ten stode +te Emperour yn full gret stude.  CMMIRK-M34,37.1061

And soo he dyd.  CMMIRK-M34,37.1070

So when +tat he was folowed +ter anon yn +te watyr, +te lepull felle

CMMIRK-M34,38.1074

and for +tys o+ter man dyd mercy, he had mercy and grace, bo+te her and

<heading>

10.  CMMIRK-M34,38.1079

DE FESTO SANCTI THOME, MARTIRIS ET EIUS SOLEMPNITATE.  CMMIRK-M34,38.1080

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, +tat ben ytaght by Goddys lawes forto come +tys
day to holy chyrch, forto worschip God and +tys holy martyr Seynt Thomas
+tat was slayn for +te lawes of holy chyrch and for +te ryght of +te rem.
CMMIRK-M34,38.1082

This holy Seynt Thomas was born yn +te cyte of London, CMMIRK-M34,38.1083

and had a fadyr was callet Gylbert, +tat was scheryue of London.
CMMIRK-M34,38.1084

+Ten felle hit, as +tys Gylbert went to +te holy lond, he was taken and

+Ten come +ter a worschypfull woman of +te contrey to hym
CMMIRK-M34,38.1086

out of his doses.  CMMIRK-M34,38.1087

+Ten was scho glad CMMIRK-M34,38.1101

CMMIRK-M34,39.1111

But bytwen Astyr and Whyssentyde Thomas made reparayle hyt a+geyne;
CMMIRK-M34,39.1112

here his felow speke for dount of strokes.  CMMIRK-M34,39.1113

For $+ter $as {TEXT:+teras} +te kyng had be+gonde +te see mony castellys

CMMIRK-M34,39.1120

He was monfull yn howshold, +tat hys hall was yche day of +te +gere new

CMMIRK-M34,39.1123

CMMIRK-M34,39.1124

11.  CMMIRK-M34,44.1281

DE CIRCUMCISIONE DOMINI NOSTRI, IHESU CRISTI.  CMMIRK-M34,44.1282

<$$heading>

Goddys owne seruandys, as +ge know well, +tys day ys called
New-+gerus-day, as endyng of +te +ger +tat ys gon, and begynnyng of
+te +gere +tat ys comyng.  Wherfor, as I hope, +ge ben comen as +tys
day to holy chyrch, forto contynue your seruice forth +tys +gere als
well o+ter bettyr +tat comy+te, as +ge dyddyn +te +gere +tat ys gon,
wythouten any new cownant makyng.  CMMIRK-M34,44.1284

For a good seruand +tat hath a good maystyr, he maketh but onys cownant
wyth hym, CMMIRK-M34,44.1285

maystyr +tat he woll for his good seruyce reward at hys ende <P_45>
and at his nede.  CMMIRK-M34,45.1286

fonte when +tay ben jcrystenet.  CMMIRK-M34,45.1287

for euermore, yn ych place, deth sewe+t hym redy, forto falle on hym,
what tyme, ny wher, he wot neuer.  CMMIRK-M34,47.1336

The fyfte ys forto +tenke, how horryble deth ys when he come+te;
CMMIRK-M34,47.1337

for yn schort tyme, he makyth hym forto stynke, +tat all hys best frendes
ben besy, forto put yn +te er+te, and hyde hym +ter.  CMMIRK-M34,47.1338

The syxte ys forto +tenke, how rew+tefull ys +te partyng of +te sowle
from +te body +tat may not be departyd, tyll +te hert yn +te body breke,
for syghtes +tat the sowle se+te.  CMMIRK-M34,47.1339

The seuent ys forto +tenke, how dredfull ys +te dome +tat he goth to.
CMMIRK-M34,47.1340

Anon +ten he +tat +tenkyth bysely on +tes seuen dayes, he schall be
circumcyset yn +te +geght day, +tat ys to say, he schall kytte away
from hym +te lust of his flesche and worldes lykyng; and so schall he
come to +te vtas of Cryst, +tat ys, to +te joy +tat ys yn heuen-blys.
To +te whech joye God bryng you and me to, +gif hit be hys wyll.
CMMIRK-M34,47.1341

Amen.  CMMIRK-M34,47.1342

12.  CMMIRK-M34,47.1344

DE EPIPHANIA DOMINI SERMO BREUIS.  CMMIRK-M34,47.1345

<$$heading>

Goddys worschypfull seruantys, as +ge knoe+te all, +tis day +ge calleth
Twelfeday.  CMMIRK-M34,47.1347

But all mys; CMMIRK-M34,47.1348

+tat a sterre shuld spryng of Iacob; CMMIRK-M34,48.1356

He was also schowet at his foloyng.  CMMIRK-M34,50.1422

<heading>

13.  CMMIRK-M34,52.1462

DE CONUERCIONE SANCTI PAULI CMMIRK-M34,52.1463

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, suche a day +ge schull haue a hegh fest yn holy
chyrch +tat ys callet +te conuersyon of Saynt Pole; +tat ys yn Englysche :
+te conuertyng of Seynt Pole.  CMMIRK-M34,52.1465

For +tat day, he was conuerted from a curset tyrand ynto Goddys seruant ,
from an hegh man and a prowde ynto a meke man and a devot, and from +te
deuellys dyssypull ynto Goddys holy apostoll.  CMMIRK-M34,52.1466

Soo, for +tis man was so yturnet from all wyckednesse ynto all goodnesse ,
yn gret streng+te and helpe to holy chyrch, +terfor holy chyrch halewo+te
his conuersyon.  CMMIRK-M34,52.1467

And soo +tay do+te of non o+ter seynt, <P_53> but only of hym.
CMMIRK-M34,53.1468

And +tat ys for +tre skylles: furst for gret myracull yn hys turnyng,
and for gret joy yn his defendyng, and for hegh ensampull in amendyng.
CMMIRK-M34,53.1469

Furst +tys man or he was turnet, he was callet Sawle.  CMMIRK-M34,53.1470

For ryght as Saule, +te kyng of Ierusalem, pursued Dauid, to haue
slayne hym, ryght soo +tis Saule pursewet Cryst, and his dyscyples, and
his seruantys, to haue broght hom to +te de+te.  Wherfor, whill Crist
+gode on erth here, he wold neuer come to hym, forto here his techyng.
CMMIRK-M34,53.1471

But as sone as he was styed ynto Heuen, +ten anon - for he was lerede
and cowthe +te Iewes lawe - he began to a+geynesette Crystys dyscipuls,
dysputyng a+geynes hom, and pursuyng hom yn all +tat {in} he myght,
in full entent to haue destryed Crystys lawes.  CMMIRK-M34,53.1472

Then, on a day, he dysputyth wyth Seynt Steven; CMMIRK-M34,53.1473

and for he myght not ouercome hym, he schaped how he myght bryng hym to
+te deth, so +tat he laft hym neuer tyll +tat he was stenet to +te dethe.
CMMIRK-M34,53.1474

+Ten, as hit ys +te maner of +te fendys chyldyr when +tay haue don a
foule turne, +tay reioysen hom +teryn, CMMIRK-M34,53.1475

and ben fayne and prowde yn hor hertys, CMMIRK-M34,53.1476

and encresen yn hor maleyse, CMMIRK-M34,53.1477

so was +tys Sawle glad of +te de+te of Seynt Steven.  CMMIRK-M34,53.1478

And for he wold haue geten hym a name of wykednesse passyng all o+ter,
he +geode to hom +tat haden +te lawe of Iewes to kepe, CMMIRK-M34,53.1479

and gete hym lettyrs of warant, forto take and bryng all crysten men
and woymen +tat +tay myght fynde yn any place, and bryng hom bonden ynto
Ierusalem, forto take hor deth +ter.  CMMIRK-M34,53.1480

And when he had +tos letteres, he toke suche a pryde, and such envy
yn his hert a+geyn cristen men, +tat when he herd speke of hom, anon
he snorted at +te nose, and fro+te at +te mowth for angur, thretyng and
manassyng so hely toward hom, +tat yche man was wondyr sor aferde of hym.
CMMIRK-M34,53.1481

Then, for he herd +tat yn +te cyte of Damaske wer mony crysten men hud
for drede, anon he toke hys hors and his men wyth hym, CMMIRK-M34,53.1482

and rode +tedyrward in all +te hast.  CMMIRK-M34,53.1483

But +ten our Lord Ihesu Crist - blessed mote he be!  - schewed +te
swetnes of his grace +tus.  CMMIRK-M34,53.1484

When +tys Saule was yn his pryde and malys, and yn purpos forto haue don
most males and harme; +ten aboute mydday, when +te sonne schone allur
clerust, then Crist cast a lyght of grace aboute Saule +tat was ferre
bryghtyr +ten +te sonne; CMMIRK-M34,53.1485

and <P_54> yn +tat lyght spak +tus to hym:'Saule, Saule, qwhy pursues
+tou me? 'CMMIRK-M34,54.1486

+Ten anon he was so sore aferd, +tat he fell downe of his hors,
CMMIRK-M34,54.1487

and for gret fere sayde:'Lord, whad art +tou? 'CMMIRK-M34,54.1488

'CMMIRK-M34,54.1489

He sayde not: I am God of Heuen, ne Goddys sonne of Heuen.
CMMIRK-M34,54.1490

But for crysten men byleven +tat Ihesu was rysen from deth to lyue,
+terfor Saule pursued most hom CMMIRK-M34,54.1491

and sayde +tat +tay leuedon on a ded mon.  CMMIRK-M34,54.1492

Herfore oure Lord Ihesu sayde:'I am Ihesu of Na+gareth';
CMMIRK-M34,54.1493

for +tat ys +te name of monhode.  CMMIRK-M34,54.1494

Then leued Saule yn hym CMMIRK-M34,54.1495

and sayde:'Lord, what wold +tou make me? 'CMMIRK-M34,54.1496

+Ten sayde Ihesu, our Lord:'Ryse and go ynto +te cyte, and +ter schall

Then seen his men +tys lyght, CMMIRK-M34,54.1498

and herden +te voyce, CMMIRK-M34,54.1499

but +tay seen no man; CMMIRK-M34,54.1500

And +ten he went ynto +te tempull, CMMIRK-M34,54.1515

CMMIRK-M34,54.1516

CMMIRK-M34,54.1517

Thus, good men, +ge mo se and here how gret a myracull God schewet yn
his conuertyng.  CMMIRK-M34,54.1518

Holy chyrche maketh alsoo gret joy for hys defendyng.  CMMIRK-M34,54.1519

Hit was gret gladnesse to all cristen men forto see hym +tat was so

And $+ter $as {TEXT:+teras} no man durst preche Goddys worde for hym,

but opynly preched +te faythe of Ihesu Crist yn iche place.
CMMIRK-M34,55.1523

And he +tat was soo prowde byfor, aftyr fell to yche crysten mannys fote

CMMIRK-M34,55.1527

CMMIRK-M34,55.1528

and soo ys taken.  CMMIRK-M34,55.1529

He was set also for ensampull of heg amendyng.  CMMIRK-M34,55.1534

CMMIRK-M34,55.1535

but he woll +tat all men and woymen ben sauet.  Wherfor, yn hegh

CMMIRK-M34,55.1536

For +tagh a man o+ter woman haue don neuer so moch a synne or lyued

CMMIRK-M34,55.1537

CMMIRK-M34,55.1539

'But +tou +tat says so, be +tou war +tat +tou lese not +tyself.
CMMIRK-M34,55.1540

+te deueles seruant +ten Goddys, +tou dampnes +tiself, CMMIRK-M34,55.1541

and art cause of +tyn owne <P_56> damp-nacyon. 'Wherfor to suche, God
ha+te ordeynt to turment fendes, and $bryng hom to +te payne +tat ha+te

penaunce in party here, CMMIRK-M34,56.1543

and so aftyr hor de+te contynue+te for+te.  Wherfor I telle +tis
ensampull +tat was told me of suche +tat knewyn hit done yn dede.
CMMIRK-M34,56.1544

Narracio.  CMMIRK-M34,56.1546

<$$heading>

Ther was a man, a curset lyuer, +tat was an officer to a lord.
CMMIRK-M34,56.1548

And as he rode to a maner of +te lordes, he fell wod, CMMIRK-M34,56.1549

and so vnbrydylt his hors +tat bare hym into a maner of +te lordes.
CMMIRK-M34,56.1550

But when he come yn, anon +te bayly sagh what +te man ayled,
CMMIRK-M34,56.1551

and made anon his hynes bynd hym to a post yn +te berne.
CMMIRK-M34,56.1552

Then when +te bayly had ysoupyd, he bade on of his hynes go and loke
how +tys man dyd.  CMMIRK-M34,56.1553

And when he come to +te berne, he segh +tre grete doggus as blacke as
a cole on yche a syde plucke away hys flesche.  CMMIRK-M34,56.1554

+Ten was +tys hyne so sore aferd, +tat vnne+te he huld hys wytte, but
+gode to his bed, and lay seke +ter longe aftyr.  CMMIRK-M34,56.1555

But, on +te morow, when men comen to +te berne, +tay fonden no mor of
+tys man, but his bare bonys and all +te flesche away.  CMMIRK-M34,56.1556

Thus who so lyueth a fowle lyfe, he may be sure of a foule ende.
CMMIRK-M34,56.1557

And +tagh his ende be fayre to mannys syght, hyt ys ryght fowle yn Goddys
syght and all his angeles.  Wherfor ych man take good ensampull, whyll

of amendyng; CMMIRK-M34,56.1558

for aftyr +tat a man ys ded, +ter nys no tyme of amendyng.
CMMIRK-M34,56.1559

And he +tat soo do+te, he schall come to Saynt Paule and haue +te ioye

his wyll.  CMMIRK-M34,56.1560

14.  CMMIRK-M34,56.1563

DE PURIFICACIONE BEATE MARIE ET EIUS SOLEMPNITATE.  CMMIRK-M34,56.1564

<$$heading>

Good cristen men and woymen, +tat louy+te to serve oure lady, and to
fast hur euens bred and watyr in hegh mede to you, <P_57> such a day +ge
schull haue Candylmasse-day; wherfor do+te in +tat euen as your deuocyon
teche+te you.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1566

For, +tat day, holy chyrche maketh gret melody yn worschyppe of hyr and
of hyr swete sonne Ihesu Crist, our Lord, specyaly yn +tre +tynges:
yn our lady puryfiyng, in Symones metyng, and yn candels offryng.
CMMIRK-M34,57.1567

This day, good men, is called +te puryfycacyon of our lady; +tat ys yn
Englyssche tong, +te clansyng of oure lady; CMMIRK-M34,57.1568

for no nede +tat scho had, CMMIRK-M34,57.1569

for scho was clansed so wyth +te worchyng of +te Holy Gost yn conceyvyng
of hur sonne, +tat +ter was laft yn hir no mater of synne, ne of non
othyr ful+te.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1570

But for +tat day was +te fourty fro +te byrthe of hyr sonne, and was
called yn +te Iewes lawe +te day of purgacion not only of oure lady,
but for all o+ter wymen of +te lawe; wherfor +get we callen hit +te
puryficacyon of our lady.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1571

The lawe of the Iewes was +ten suche +tat a woman +tat was delyuerde
of a man-chyld sculd be holden vnclene by +te lawe VII dayes aftyr hur
burth; CMMIRK-M34,57.1572

and +ten +te lawe +gaf hur leue to go to hur husbondys bed.
CMMIRK-M34,57.1573

But +get scho was vnclene by +te lawe +tre and xxx=ti= dayes aftyr,
so +tat tyll fourty dayes wer fulfylled, scho schuld not come wythyn
+te temple.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1574

+Ten, +tat day, scho schuld come to +te tempull wyth hyr offryng and wyth
hur sonne, and offre for a ryche man a lombe, and for a pore a payre of
turturs o+ter two culuer-bryddes.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1575

And soo offred oure lady for hyr sonne.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1576

And yf a woman wer delyuerd of a mayden-chyld, scho schuld dowbull +te
dayes of comyng to chyrch, and to hur husbonddys bed, and comyng ynto
+te tempull.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1577

For, as clerkes techen, hit ys VII dayes aftyr a woman conseyueth of
+te man, er +tan +te sede turne ynto blod; and +tre and +trytty dayes
aftyr +tat +ten, or hit haue shap of man: CMMIRK-M34,57.1578

and +ten God sendyth lyfe ynto hit.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1579

And yf hit be a maydechylde, hit dowbulth all +te dayes, bo+te of turnyng
ynto blod, and ynto schappe of body.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1580

And +tys ys +te cause +tat for encheson +tat +te forme woman Eue vexude
God more +ten dyd man, +terfor scho ys more lengyr yn formyng +ten
+te man.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1581

+Tus for fleschly coupull of man and woman ys vnclene yn hymselfe,
+terfor lawe ordeyneth a remedy forto clanse hom.  CMMIRK-M34,57.1582

But +ten +ge schull know wele +tat oure lady had no nede to +tys <P_58>
clansying, CMMIRK-M34,58.1583

for scho conceyuet not of coupull of man but only of +te Holy Gost,
so +tat scho was clene of all maner fulthe towchyng conseyt of man.
CMMIRK-M34,58.1584

Neuer+teles, scho +gode to +te tempull as o+ter woymen dydden for foure
skylles.  CMMIRK-M34,58.1585

The fyrst was to fulfyll scripture +tat bydde+te +tus:'+Te grettyr +tou
be, +te meker make +te yn all +tyng'; CMMIRK-M34,58.1586

+tus scho dyd.  CMMIRK-M34,58.1587

For +tagh scho wyst +tat scho was modyr to Goddys Sonne of Heuen, and
was so full of worschyp passyng all othyr woymen, +get scho made hur as
+te porest woman +tat was yn hur company.  CMMIRK-M34,58.1588

The secunde skyll was to fulfyll +te lawe.  CMMIRK-M34,58.1589

For ry+gt as scho fulfylled +te lawe yn +te circumcysyon of hur sonne ,
ryght soo scho fulfyllet hit yn hur puryficacyon and offryng of hur
sonne yn +te tempull, doyng for hym as o+tir pore woymen dydden for
hor chyldyrn.  CMMIRK-M34,58.1590

The +trid skylle was forto stoppe mowthes, lest +tay had sayde +tat
+tay dyd not +te lawe, and soo cast a gret chalange a+geyns hom yn tyme
comyng +teraftyr.  CMMIRK-M34,58.1591

The fowrth skylle was to ensampull to all cristen woymen +tat +tay
schuld come to +te chyrche aftyr hor burth, and +tonke God heghly +tat
had saued hom hole and sonde yn hor trauayle; CMMIRK-M34,58.1592

for +ter nys non euel +tat go+te so nygh +te de+te wyth scapyng as
do+te hit.  CMMIRK-M34,58.1593

For +tes skylles God made mynde of our lady purefiyng.  CMMIRK-M34,58.1594

He made also mynde of Symones and Anne a+geyncomyng.  CMMIRK-M34,58.1595

+Tys Symeon was a passyng old man; CMMIRK-M34,58.1596

but for he prayde besely day and nyght to God +tat he most see Cryst
bodely, er +ten he deyd, and soo God grawnted hym his bone, and +tis
Anne also, not Anne, our ladyes modyr, but ano+ter +tat was weddyd
seven +gere, and +ten when hur husband was ded, scho lyued tyll scho
was foure skore +gere old, and serued God yn +te tempull day and nyght.
CMMIRK-M34,58.1597

+Tat also +tat had grawnte of God to see Crist er scho deyd.
CMMIRK-M34,58.1598

Then when our lady come toward +te tempull wyt hor sonne, +te Holy Gost
warnet +tys Symeon and +tys Anne; CMMIRK-M34,58.1599

and +tay +ter wyth mecull ioye +gode a+geynes hom, CMMIRK-M34,58.1600

and broght hom ynto +te tempull.  CMMIRK-M34,58.1601

+Ten Symeon toke hym yn his armes wyth all +te reuerens +tat he cow+te,
CMMIRK-M34,58.1602

and cussed hym, CMMIRK-M34,58.1603

and +tonked hym heghly +tat he let hym lyue to +te tyme forto se hym
bodely wyth his een.  Wherfor, +get yn mynde of +tys processe, when a
woman cometh <P_59> to +te chyrche-dyrre tyll +te pryst come and cast

For and scho haue ben at hys bed befor, scho most take hor penance and
he, bothe.  CMMIRK-M34,59.1605

+Terfor holy chyrch maketh mynde +tys day of candels offryng.
CMMIRK-M34,59.1606

+Ge seen, good men, +tat hyt ys comyn vse to all crysten men forto come
to +te chyrche +tys day, and bere a candyll yn processyon, as +tagh
+tay +gedyn bodyly wyth oure lady to chyrch, and aftyr offyr wyth hyr
yn worschip and high reuerens of hur.  CMMIRK-M34,59.1607

Then now hereth how +tys worschip was furst yfond, when +te Romaynes by
gret chyualry conquerod all +te world.  CMMIRK-M34,59.1608

For +tay wern euerous yn hor doyng +tat retten not to God of Heuen +tat
+gaf hom +tat euere; CMMIRK-M34,59.1609

but made hom dyuerse goddys, aftyr hor owne lust.  CMMIRK-M34,59.1610

And soo, among othyr, +tay hadden a god +tat was callet Mars, +tat
was byfor +tat tyme a chyualrous knyght, and an euerous yn batayle.
Wherfor +tay called hym god of batayle, prayng +gorne to hym for helpe.
CMMIRK-M34,59.1611

And for +tay wolden spede +te bettyr, +tay dyd gret worschyp to his modyr
+tat was callet Februa; aftyr +te whech woman, as mony haue opynyon,
+tys mon +tat now ys was called February.  Wherfor +te fyrst day of
+tys mone +tat now ys Candylmasse-day, +te Romans wold goo al nyght
about +te cyte of Rome wyth torches, and blasus and canduls brennyng,

ray+tyr helpe of hyr sonne Mars yn hor doyng.  CMMIRK-M34,59.1612

Then was +ter a pope +tat heght Sergyus.  CMMIRK-M34,59.1613

For he segh cristen men drawe to thys mawmetry, he +toght to turne
+tat foule custom ynto Goddys worschyp and oure lady Seynt Mary,
CMMIRK-M34,59.1614

and commaundyd all cristen men and wymmen forto come +tys same day to

and hur swete sonne.  CMMIRK-M34,59.1615

Soo yche man aftyr, by processe of tyme, lafton +tat worschip +tat +tay
dyden to +tat woman Februa, CMMIRK-M34,59.1616

and duden worschip to our lady and to hyr sonne, so +tat now +tys
solempnyte ys halowed +trogh crystendame, CMMIRK-M34,59.1617

and yche man, and woman, and chyld of age come+te +tys day to +te chyrche,
CMMIRK-M34,59.1618

and offren brennyng condyls; as +togh +tay wer bodyly wyth our lady to

yn er+te, to haue a gret reward +terfor yn Heuen.  CMMIRK-M34,60.1619

And so +tay may be sure +terof.  CMMIRK-M34,60.1620

For a candyll brennyng bytokenyth oure lady, and hor sonne, and a man
hymselfe; CMMIRK-M34,60.1621

for a candyll ys made of whyte weke and of wax brennyng wyth fyre.
CMMIRK-M34,60.1622

+Tus Crystys whyt soule was hydde wyth his monhede CMMIRK-M34,60.1623

and brenne+te wyth +te fyre of his Godhed; CMMIRK-M34,60.1624

hit bytokenyth also our ladyys modyrhode and maydynhede, lightnet wyth
+te fyre of loue; CMMIRK-M34,60.1625

hyt bytokeneth also yche good man and woman +tat do+te good dedes wyth

Wherfor yf any of you ha+te soo trespassyd to his neghtbur wherby +tat
+tys candyll of charyte ys qwenchet, furst go he and acord hym wyth his
neghtbur, and so tend his condyll a+geyne, and +ten offyr his condyll
to +te pryst.  CMMIRK-M34,60.1626

For +tys ys Godys commaundment; CMMIRK-M34,60.1627

and elles he lesyth hys meryt of his offryng.  CMMIRK-M34,60.1628

Narracio.  CMMIRK-M34,60.1630

<$$heading>

I rede yn +te lyfe of Saynt Dunstan how +tat his modyr, when scho was
gret wyth chyld wyth hym, scho come on Condylmasseday to +te chyrch.
CMMIRK-M34,60.1632

And when all +te pepull had gon on processyon wyth candyls brennyng, and
stoden all yn +te chyrche, yche on wyth his lyght yn hys hond, sodenly
all the condyls +tat wern yn +te chyrche wern quaynt, CMMIRK-M34,60.1633

and a gret derkenes come wyth all, so +tat vnneth on myght se ano+ter.
CMMIRK-M34,60.1634

And when +tay haden stond soo long sore aferd, +ten come +ter a fayre
lyght from Heuen, CMMIRK-M34,60.1635

and lyght +te candyll +tat Saynt Dunstanys modyr had yn hond;
CMMIRK-M34,60.1636

and so offryd hyr condyll.  CMMIRK-M34,60.1637

And so of hure al o+ter werne lyght, so +tat wythyn a whyle aftyr,
all +te chyrche was so lyght a+geyne, yn token he was yn hyr wombe +tat
schuld aftyr tynd mony mannys charite, +tat was befor qwenchet by envy.
CMMIRK-M34,60.1638

<heading>

Narracio.  CMMIRK-M34,60.1640

<$$heading>

I rede of anothyr woman +tat was soo deuot yn oure lady seruyce, +tat
scho +gaf for hor loue all +te clo+tys +tat scho had, saue +te febullyst
+tat scho +god yn herselfe.  CMMIRK-M34,60.1642

Hit fell so +tat on Condylmasse-day, scho wold haue goon to chyrche.
CMMIRK-M34,60.1643

But for scho was not honest arayde, scho dyrst not for schame;
CMMIRK-M34,60.1644

for scho had non <P_61> honest clo+tes, as scho was wont to haue.
CMMIRK-M34,61.1645

CMMIRK-M34,61.1646

for scho schuld be wythout masse +tat holy fest.  Wherfor scho went

CMMIRK-M34,61.1647

And so as scho prayde, scho fell on slepe, CMMIRK-M34,61.1648

and +toght +tat scho was yn a fayre chyrche, CMMIRK-M34,61.1649

and sygh a gret company of maydens comyng ynto +te chyrche; and on +tat

15.  CMMIRK-M34,62.1704

DE DOMINICA IN SEPTUAGESIMA BREUIS SERMO.  CMMIRK-M34,62.1705

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, +ge schull all know well +tat +tys day is called
Sonday yn +te Septagesin.  CMMIRK-M34,62.1707

Then for enchesen +tat holy chyrche ys modyr to all cristen pepull,
scho taketh hede to hyr chyldern as a good modyr ouyth forto do,
CMMIRK-M34,62.1708

and seyth hom all sore seke yn +te sekenes of synne, and mony of hom
wonded to de+te wyth +te swerd of synne.  +Te wheche sekenesse +tay haue
caght all +tys +gere before, but namely +tes Cristynmasse-dayes +tat
wern ordeynet in holy chyrche for gret solempnyte.  CMMIRK-M34,62.1709

For yche man schuld +tat tyme make more solempnyte, and more bysyly,
and more mekely, and more deuotly serue God +ten any o+ter <P_63>
tyme of +te +gere; for cause +tat God schewed all mankynd thelke dayes

tyme, CMMIRK-M34,63.1711

of all ful+te and vnclennes of synne, CMMIRK-M34,63.1712

doyng gret almes, yche mon aftyr hys hauyng, to hom +tat haden nede.
CMMIRK-M34,63.1713

CMMIRK-M34,63.1714

CMMIRK-M34,63.1715

+Tus +te holy dayes of +tat fest +tat wer ordeynt yn hegh worschyp to

on hym for mercy, he set vs here, to do penaunce to our lyues ende.
CMMIRK-M34,67.1826

But +ten, for suche a gret synne may not be qwaynt but wyth gret penaunce,
+te more penaunce we don, +te more ys oure mede befor God.  Wherfor go
a+geyne ynto +ty penance yn Godys name. 'CMMIRK-M34,67.1827

Eft he come a+geyne to Eue CMMIRK-M34,67.1828

+get +te +trid tyme he come a+geyne to hur CMMIRK-M34,68.1835

CMMIRK-M34,68.1837

Then +gede Eue a+geyne CMMIRK-M34,68.1851

and dud hyr penaunce mekely tyll hyr lyues ende.  CMMIRK-M34,68.1852

In tokenyng of +tys, +tis Sonday ys called'Yn Septuagesin,'+tat ys a

CMMIRK-M34,68.1857

Then scho takythe comfort to hyr yn party CMMIRK-M34,68.1858

CMMIRK-M34,68.1859

+Ten scho ley+t don tractys, and grayles, CMMIRK-M34,68.1860

<heading>

16.  CMMIRK-M34,69.1866

DE DOMINICA IN SEXAGESIMA BREUIS SERMO.  CMMIRK-M34,69.1867

<$$heading>

Goode men and woymen, +tys day ys called yn holy chirch Sonday yn
Sexagesin.  CMMIRK-M34,69.1869

+Ten +ge schull knowe well +tat Sexagesin ys sette for a nowmbur of
+tre score.  By +te whech nowmbyr +ge schull vndyrstond +tat holy chyrche
techeth yche man and woman, to +tenke on how schort a mannis lyfe is now
in our dayes o+ter +tat hit was in olde tyme before.  CMMIRK-M34,69.1870

For, summe tyme, men lyuedon IX hundyrt wyntur and more;
CMMIRK-M34,69.1871

but, now, he +tat lyuy+te +tre score +ger or summewhat more, he ys taken
for a long lyuyng man.  CMMIRK-M34,69.1872

But +te goodnes of God ys so moche, +tat yf we wyll be wyse yn our schort
lyue forto plese God and saue our soules, he woll +geue vs as moche mede
yn Heuen, as he +gaf hom +tat lyued soo mony +geres.  CMMIRK-M34,69.1873

+Ten he +tat woll haue +tat mede of God, he most haue +tre +tynges
wythe hym; +tat ys: forto suffyr tribulacyon mekly, forto do almes-dede
dyscretly, and forto hate synne namly.  CMMIRK-M34,69.1874

+Ten, for a manys dayes byn schort, he most suffyr +te more tribulacyon
wyth good wyll, and not wyth grychyng a+geyne hym.  CMMIRK-M34,69.1875

For hyt comy+te of specyall grace of God when he sendys any man
tribulacyon o+ter any dysese; CMMIRK-M34,69.1876

for hyt ys o+ter for remedy of his synnys forto haue his penance here,
o+ter yn hey encres of his joy befor God.  CMMIRK-M34,69.1877

+Ten, for Saynt Paule, Godis holy apostoll, woll +tat yche man take
ensampull by hym forto suffyr tribulacyon wyth good wyll, he rehersyth
yn +te pystyll of +tys day moche of +te tribulacyon +tat he suffyrd
CMMIRK-M34,69.1878

and saythe thus:'I haue be put ynto prison oft-tymes, and suffyrd wondys
of gret chaynes and o+ter dyuerse yrens; and fyue tymes betyn wyth
scorgys of +te Iewes, and had yche tyme nene and +trytty strokes on my
bare body; <P_70> and +tryse beton wyth +gardys of paynones; and onys
beton wyth stons; and +tryse ben yn schipwrak on +te see, and was yn +te
grond of +te see on nyght and on day; and ofte-tyme in pareyle of flodys,
and yn pareyl of +teves, and yn pareyle of fals bre+tern +tat schewedon
hom to me louyng and trewe, and werne false and entyset o+ter to do me
doses. 'CMMIRK-M34,70.1879

He rehersyth all +te woo +tat he suffyrd yn dyuerse trauayls, yn
myscheves, yn colde, yn nakedschip, yn +turst, yn hongur, yn long wakyng,
yn fastyng, and yn mony o+ter myscheves +tat he suffurd, +tat wern to
long to tell.  CMMIRK-M34,70.1880

And all he suffyrd wyth good wyll, CMMIRK-M34,70.1881

and euer +tonked God of hys swete sonde; CMMIRK-M34,70.1882

for wele he wyst +tat all +te doses +tat God send to hym, was for syn
+tat he dyd befor, and for encrese of his meryt aftyr.  Wherfor yche man
+tat will plese God - what maner doses come+te to hym, be hit sekenes
, be hit lose of goodys +tat ben worldly, o+ter deth of any frende -
take hyt as esely as +ge may; CMMIRK-M34,70.1883

for in tyme aftyr when he is maystyr of hymselfe, +ten +tonke he God
CMMIRK-M34,70.1884

and pray hym mekely of mercy of his ynpaciens.  CMMIRK-M34,70.1885

God knowe+te your fragelte, CMMIRK-M34,70.1886

and +terfor he for+geueth sone all +to +tat askyth hym mercy wyth a
meke hert.  CMMIRK-M34,70.1887

+Tus most a man suffyr tribulacyon mekely.  CMMIRK-M34,70.1888

He most also do almys-dede dyscretly, +te wheche byn fyguret by +tes
Syxagesin +tat byn syxty dayes.  CMMIRK-M34,70.1889

For syxty ys syx tymys ten, so +tat by +te syx +ge schull vndyrstond +te
syx werkes of charyte +tat comen out of +te ten commawndementys of God.
+Te whech werkes byn: forto +gyue mete to +te hongry; forto +geue drynke
to +te +tursty; to clo+te hom +tat byn acold for defaute of clo+tes;
forto +geue hom herber +tat hauen non; forto help hom +tat byn seke
of +tat hom nedyth; forto viset presoners, and socour hom wyth mete,
and drynke, and o+ter +tat hom nedyth; CMMIRK-M34,70.1890

and othyr werke holy chyrch layth to; +tat ys: forto bury +te pore +tat
ha+te no helpe as Toby dude.  CMMIRK-M34,70.1891

+Tys ben +te werkes of charite and of mercy +te whech ych man and woman
most nedely do, +tat wyll haue mercy of God yn +te dredfull day of dome.
Wherfor +tis Sexagesin bygynnyth +tys day and endyth +te Wonnysday yn
Astyr-weke; +te wheche holy chyrche syngu+te:'Venite benedicti Patrys
mei etc.,'that ys in Englysche:'Com +ge, my fadyrys blessed
chyldyrne, and takyth +te kyndome of Heuen +tat ys ordeynt to you.
'CMMIRK-M34,70.1892

Thes same wordys God schall say to you at +te day of dome <P_71> and
to all +tat han don +te werkes of mercy dyscretly.  Wherfor all +tat
han wherof, +tay moten do hom yn dede; and +tay +tat haue not wherof,
+tay moten haue good wylle forto do, yf +tay hadyn wherof; so +tat hor
good wyll schall fulfyll +tat hor nonpower may not.  CMMIRK-M34,71.1893

Then, for +tes werkes moten be don dyscretly, lest a man lese all yfere,
God techythe by ensampull yn +te gospell of +tys day how +tay schull be
don CMMIRK-M34,71.1894

and seythe +tus:'A mon +gode out, forto sowe his sede; CMMIRK-M34,71.1895

and when he sew, som sede fell by +te way, CMMIRK-M34,71.1896

and fowles of +te ayre etyn hit; CMMIRK-M34,71.1897

and som fell on a stone, CMMIRK-M34,71.1898

and hit dryet vp for defaute of humore; CMMIRK-M34,71.1899

and somme fell among +tornes, CMMIRK-M34,71.1900

and hoo in +te grownde choket hit; CMMIRK-M34,71.1901

and som fell yn good erthe, CMMIRK-M34,71.1902

and hyt bro+gt furthe frute an hundyrthfold. 'CMMIRK-M34,71.1903

This way say+te Cryst:'I am +te way to Heuen. 'Wherfor his sede fallyth
bysyde +te way, +tat +geue+te hys almes not only for Crystys loue, but
for pompe of +te world, and vayn glory, and forto be holden a holy man;
and so lesy+te al yfere.  CMMIRK-M34,71.1904

Narracio.  CMMIRK-M34,71.1906

<$$heading>

I rede +tat +ter was a wondyr $rych {TEXT:ry_h} man, som tyme, yn Eirlond,
CMMIRK-M34,71.1908

and dyd so mony almys-dedys yn hys lyue, +tat all men wendon +tat he
had ben a gret seynt before God.  CMMIRK-M34,71.1909

But when he was ded, he apered to won +tat loued hym wele yn his lyue,
as blak as pyche wyth an horrybull stenche, CMMIRK-M34,71.1910

and sayde to hym:'+ge wenyn I am a saynt; CMMIRK-M34,71.1911

but now I am such as +tou may se. 'CMMIRK-M34,71.1912

'CMMIRK-M34,71.1913

+Ten sayde he:'+Te wynd of vayn glorye hathe blowen hom away.
'CMMIRK-M34,71.1914

Thus he +tat do+te almys-dedys for vayne glorie, he lesyth all his mede
, CMMIRK-M34,71.1915

and fendys of +te ayre strien hit.  CMMIRK-M34,71.1916

His sede fallyth on a stone, +tat +geuyth his almys to suche as he
knoweth well, +tat ben groundyd in dedly synne and woll not leue hit,
CMMIRK-M34,71.1917

or whosoo mantaynyth hom yn hor synne, he lesy+te his mede.
CMMIRK-M34,71.1918

His sede also +tat fallyth among +tornes, +tat +geuyth hys almes to ryche
men +tat haue no nede +terto, and also +geuyth hit to his seruandys in
reward of hor hyre, and soo lesyth hys mede.  CMMIRK-M34,71.1919

But his sede fally+te yn good erthe, +tat +geueth his almes to good, pore,
trew men +tat ben Godys ayr, and othyr wher +ter he wot, hit ys almes.
CMMIRK-M34,71.1920

And +tys sede schall +geld a hundrethfold fruyt, and be euerlastyng fode
yn <P_72> Heuen.  CMMIRK-M34,72.1921

+Tus +ge +tat don almes dyscretly, schull haue +gour fode yn Heuen
perpetuall.  CMMIRK-M34,72.1922

He most also hate syn namely, and sle hit yn all +tat he may;
CMMIRK-M34,72.1923

for he +tat hatyth synne, louyth God, CMMIRK-M34,72.1924

and God louyth hym; CMMIRK-M34,72.1925

and so he is made on spyryte wyth God.  CMMIRK-M34,72.1926

God hatyth synne so moche, +tat he toke vengeans on all +te world, as
holy chyrche nowe makyth mynde, and namely for synne of $lechery and of
vowtrye, and for synne a+geyne kynd.  CMMIRK-M34,72.1927

Then, for God segh +tis wikednes namly of +tes synnys regnyng yn +te
world, he sayde +tus:'Me forthenkyth +tat I made man. 'Wherfor he sayde
to Noye:'All +te world ys enfect wyth synne so greuesly, +tat I woll
strye hit wyth a flod.  Wherfor make +te a schyppe, as I woll teche
+te, of planke-bordes, and make chambors +teryn, and take of all clene
bestys +tre coupull and on by hymself of all o+ter vnclene bestys take
on cowpull yn, and mete wyth hom. 'CMMIRK-M34,72.1928

Then made Noye +tys schyppe as God taght hym, sqware in +te bo+tom, of
+tre hundyrt cubytes yn lengthe, and yn brede fyfty cubytys, and +trytty
cubites yn heght; so +tat +tis schippe was yn makyng a hundyrt wyntyr,
forto schew how mercyable God ys, and how lo+te he ys to do vengeans.
CMMIRK-M34,72.1929

And he do+te hit, forto loke yf men wold amend and aske mercy.
CMMIRK-M34,72.1930

But for +te pepull wold not amende, but was euer +te lengyr +te worse,
al maner of bestys, as God bade byfore, werne jbroght byfore Noye by
help of +te angelys, and don yn +te schippe.  CMMIRK-M34,72.1931

And when all wern broght yn, God bade Noye and his +tre sonnes goo ynto
+te schyppe by homself; and Noyeys wyfe and hys sonnes wyues by homselfe
; for encheson +tat, yn tyme of affliccyon, men schuld absten hom from

So when +tay wern alle in, God closud +te dore aftyr hom wythout-forth ;
CMMIRK-M34,72.1933

and +ten hit rayned so gretly fourty dayes and fourty nyghtys, +tat
+te watyr bare +te schyppe herre +ten any hull by fyfty cubytys,
CMMIRK-M34,72.1934

and stod so styll an hundyrt dayes and fyfty, CMMIRK-M34,72.1935

And so was all +te world drownet, bo+te man and best, outtaken hom +tat
werne in +te schyppe.  CMMIRK-M34,72.1936

Neuer+teles Ioseph sayth +tat in Armeny ys a hull +tat ys called Baris,
+tat was herre +ten +te watyr where mony men and woymen were ysaued,
as men haue an oppynyon.  CMMIRK-M34,72.1937

+Ter was <P_73> Noye a twolfmony+te yn +te schyppe.  CMMIRK-M34,73.1938

+Ten he put out a raven forto bryng worde yf +te watyr wer all sesyd
or no.  CMMIRK-M34,73.1939

+Ten fond +tys rauen a drowned careyn, CMMIRK-M34,73.1940

and fulled hym +terof, CMMIRK-M34,73.1941

and come not a+geyne.  CMMIRK-M34,73.1942

Aftyr Noye send a culuer out +tat come a+geyne wyth a branche of an
olyue-tre in hur byll; wherby Noye knew +tat +te watyr was sesyt and
+tonkyd God heghly.  CMMIRK-M34,73.1943

Then when God bade hym go out, he +gede out, CMMIRK-M34,73.1944

and toke out +te hed-best of +te clene bestys, CMMIRK-M34,73.1945

and brent hym yn offryng to God.  Wherfor God was so wele payde +tat he
+gaf hym and all men aftyr hym leue forto ete flesche of clene bestys,
and forto drynke wyne $+ter $as {TEXT:+teras} befor +te flod men etyn
no flessche, ne drynkyd no drynke but watyr; CMMIRK-M34,73.1946

for +te erthe was so badfull byfor, +tat hom nedud non o+ter fode,
but suche as come of +te erth.  CMMIRK-M34,73.1947

+Tus, good men, +ge most vndyrstond how gret vengeans God toke on +te
world for wykednesse of synne, CMMIRK-M34,73.1948

and now, more harme ys, +te pepull ar as full of synne as +tay wer +tat
tyme; CMMIRK-M34,73.1949

and +terfor God will take vengeans, ner +te prayers of holy sayntys and
specyaly of our lady.  CMMIRK-M34,73.1950

Narracio.  CMMIRK-M34,73.1952

<$$heading>

For +tis I rede yn +te lyfe of Seynt Domink CMMIRK-M34,73.1954

when he was on a nyght yn his deuocyons he segh our Lord Ihesu holdyng

Then come our lady anon, CMMIRK-M34,73.1956

<heading>

17.  CMMIRK-M34,74.1973

DE DOMINICA IN QUINQUAGESIMA SERMO BREUIS.  CMMIRK-M34,74.1974

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, +tys day is callet yn holy chyrche Sonday yn
Quinquagesin.  CMMIRK-M34,74.1976

+Ten schull +ge know +tat +tys word quinquagesin ys an nowmbur of fyfty,
+te wheche nowmbur bytokenyth remission and ioye.  CMMIRK-M34,74.1977

For yn +te old lawe, ych fyfty wynter, all men and woymen +tat wern sette
wyth seruice and bondage, +tay wern made fre in gret ioy and murth to hom.
Wherfor +tys nowmbur bygynnyth +tys day, and endyth yn Estyrday, schewyng
+tat yche godys-seruand +tat ys oppressyd wyth tribulacyon, and takyth
hit mekely yn his hert, he schall be made fre yn his resurrecyon: +tat
ys yn +te day of dome, and be made +te ayre of +te kyndome of Heuen.
CMMIRK-M34,74.1978

And +get yn more comfort of all Godys pepull yche fyfte +gere, +te pope
of Rome graunty+te a full remyssion of all synnys to yche man and weman
+tat comyth to Rome +tat +gere.  CMMIRK-M34,74.1979

ynwardly sory for hys synnys and his gyltes; and so schryue hym clene,

Hereby +ge may know opynly how spedfull hyt ys to a man to be contrite
of his synnys.  Wherfor forto draw men to contricion namly +tes fyfty
dayes , +te fyft psalme of +te sauter, +tat ys:'Miserere mei, Deus! ' ys
more rehersyd +tes dayes +ten any o+ter tyme of +te +gere.  +Te wheche

me; and aftyr +ty multytude of +ty mercyus, do away my wickednesse!
'and soo forth.  CMMIRK-M34,76.2018

Thus when a man ys sory for hys synnys and sayth +tes wordys wyth full
hert, God heryth his prayer CMMIRK-M34,76.2019

and for+geueth hym hys trespas, so +tat he be yn full wyll to
amende hym yn tyme comyng, and also full of charyte wythout faynyng.
CMMIRK-M34,76.2020

For, what maner vertu +tat a man haue, but yf he be yn charyte, hit
stondys hym in no vayle; CMMIRK-M34,76.2021

for +togh he wepe and crye to God: whyll he ys wythout charyte to any
of hys euencristen, God heryth hym not.  CMMIRK-M34,76.2022

Herto acordyth Seynt Paule yn +te pystyll of +tys day CMMIRK-M34,76.2023

and sayth +tus:'Thagh I were as eloquent yn speche as any man or any

+tagh a man wenyth he leue+te his God and loue not hys euencristen,
he ys dysceyuet; CMMIRK-M34,76.2024

CMMIRK-M34,76.2025

Thus most a man haue full charite +tat woll be sauet befor God.
CMMIRK-M34,76.2026

For he +tat deyth yn charite, schall be sauet; CMMIRK-M34,76.2027

and he +tat deyth yn dedly synne, schall be dampnet: whefor of all

+Get +ge most haue stabull fayth wythout flateryng, so +tat +ge leue

CMMIRK-M34,76.2031

18.  CMMIRK-M34,79.2084

DE FESTO SANCTI MATHIE, APOSTOLI, ET EIUS SOLEMPNITATE.
CMMIRK-M34,79.2085

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, suche a day +ge schull haue Seynt Mathis day, Godys
holy apostull.  +Te whech ha+te non euen set yn certeyne forto fast, but

+tyng +tat he dyde.  CMMIRK-M34,79.2089

CMMIRK-M34,79.2092

+Ten Crist made hym on of hys dyscypull.  CMMIRK-M34,79.2095

Iewes for thrytty penyes.  CMMIRK-M34,79.2097

+Ten was +te pepull sore aferde of +tat syght, CMMIRK-M34,81.2165

<heading>

DE DOMINICA IN QUADRAGESIMA SERMO BREUIS.  CMMIRK-M34,82.2185

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, +tys day ys called in holy chyrch Sonday yn
Quadragesin.  CMMIRK-M34,82.2187

+Ten ys quadragesin a nowmbur of fourty; CMMIRK-M34,82.2188

for fro +tis day to Astyr ben forty dayes +tat byth +te te+tedayes of
+te +gere.  CMMIRK-M34,82.2189

And for ych man dothe forfet more o+ter las, +terfor, forto make

for nede.  CMMIRK-M34,82.2190

That ben chyldyr wythyn xxi +gere, woymen wyth chyld, old men passed

labryn sore fore hor lyuelod: CMMIRK-M34,82.2191

+tus +te lawe dyspensyth wyth apon hore concyens.  CMMIRK-M34,82.2192

+Ten for bycause +tat Sonday ys no day of fastyng, +terfor +ge schull

and take askes at +te prestys hond, and ber forth in your hert +tat he
sayth to you, when he layth askes on your hedys.  CMMIRK-M34,82.2193

+Ten he saythe +tus:'Man, thynke +tat +tou art but eskys,
CMMIRK-M34,82.2194

+Ten byn +ter +tre dyuerse skylles why +ge schull fast +tes fourty dayes.
CMMIRK-M34,82.2196

On ys, bycause as +te gospell of +tys day telly+te, how +tat +te Holy
Gost lad our Lord ynto desert +tat was bytwyx Ierusalem and Ieryco,
forto be temptyd of +te fende.  CMMIRK-M34,82.2197

CMMIRK-M34,83.2198

and lyfty+te manys hert to God, CMMIRK-M34,83.2200

and +gevyth hym vertu and mede; CMMIRK-M34,83.2201

hit +geuyth hym mede in Heuen +tat euer schall last, and uertu yn er+te

CMMIRK-M34,83.2204

CMMIRK-M34,83.2205

for gloteny ys not yn a manys mete, but yn foule appetyte.
CMMIRK-M34,83.2210

+Ten sayd Crist to hym:'A man schall not only lyue by bred; but yche
word +tat go+te out of Godys mow+te. 'CMMIRK-M34,83.2211

+Ten +te fende toke Crist, CMMIRK-M34,83.2212

+tat I may know +te for Godys sonne. 'CMMIRK-M34,83.2214

CMMIRK-M34,83.2215

+get, +te +tryd tyme, he toke hym, CMMIRK-M34,83.2216

'CMMIRK-M34,83.2219

+Ten +te fende lafte hym, CMMIRK-M34,83.2222

+Tus +ge schull a+geynes gloteny.  CMMIRK-M34,84.2243

+ge schull put away all euell +toghtes of heghnes, and haue +toghtys

+Tenky+te how a man ys borne febull, and seke, and naked, and pore;

<heading>

20.  CMMIRK-M34,86.2263

DE DOMINICA PRIMA QUADRAGESIME.  CMMIRK-M34,86.2264

<$$heading>

Hortamur vos, ne in vacuum graciam Dei recipiatis.  Corintheos VI=to=.
CMMIRK-M34,86.2266

Good men and woymen, +tes wordes +tat I haue sayde yn Lateyn, byn +tus
to say yn Englysch:'We amonechen you, +tat +ge take not +te grace of
God yn vayn. 'CMMIRK-M34,86.2267

+Tes ben +te wordes of Seynt Paule, Cristys holy apostull, +tat ben
red yn +te pystyll of +tys day; by +te wheche word +tys holy apostull
chargyth all good pepull, +tat +tay take hede what grace God sendyth hom,
and +tat +tay taken not +tat grace yn vayn.  CMMIRK-M34,86.2268

God +geuyth grace to man all tymes; CMMIRK-M34,86.2269

but for a man nedy+te more hys grace +tys tyme +ten ano+ter, +terfor,
of hys hegh mercy, he +geuyth now-dayes more habundant of Lenton +ten
any o+ter tyme.  The whech grace he partu+te yn +tre wayes, +tat ys to
say: in way of gracyous abydyng, in way of gracyous demyng, and yn way
of gracyous amendys makyng.  CMMIRK-M34,86.2270

+Tes +tre wayes God sendyth hys grace to you now.  Wherfor, ryght as
Seynt Paule monysche+te hys dyscypuls, ryght soo I monyssch you +tat
ben my chyldyr yn God, +tat +ge take not +tys grace of God yn vayn.
CMMIRK-M34,86.2271

+Ge haue a comyn sayng among you, CMMIRK-M34,86.2272

and sayn +tat Godys grace ys worth a new fayre.  CMMIRK-M34,86.2273

+Ten takyth hede how moche worth Godys grace ys; CMMIRK-M34,86.2274

for +tagh any of you had as moche gold as a fayre ys worth, but he had
Godys grace wyth hyt, hyt schuld turne hym more ynto schenschip +ten
ynto worschyp.  CMMIRK-M34,86.2275

+Tus +ge may se by veray reson +tat Godys grace ys more wor+ty +ten
any fayre.  CMMIRK-M34,86.2276

But +get +ge schull know for+ter, CMMIRK-M34,86.2277

for, +tagh a man had neuer soo moche riches and prorperyte here +tat
comyth all of Godys grace, but yf he take +tat grace wele and ples his
God wythall, hyt schall turne hym ynto dampnacyon.  CMMIRK-M34,86.2278

But for +te pore playnyth on +te ryche, and sayn +tay ben vnkynd to God,
and don not as God byddyth hom doo, and full eldyr seen a mote yn ano+ter
manys ee +tat con not se a beem yn hor one: +terfor +ge schall knowe
wele +tat hyt ys a specyall grace of God, when he makyth a man ryche
and som mon pore.  CMMIRK-M34,86.2279

He maky+te hom rych, +tat +tay wyth hor ryches schuld socour +te pore
yn hor nede, and soo wyth hor good <P_87> by hom Heuen; CMMIRK-M34,87.2280

and som he makyth pore, +tat hor pouerte schall be hor saluacyon.
CMMIRK-M34,87.2281

For God knowe+te wele, yf +tay wern rych, +tay wold for+gete hor God , and
soo spyll homselfe.  Wherfor we amonyschen yow, bo+te ryche and pore, +tat
+ge take not +tys grace of God yn ydull nor yn vayn.  CMMIRK-M34,87.2282

But he +tat is rych, set not hys hert +terapon; CMMIRK-M34,87.2283

but euer be yn drede, lest he myspend hit, CMMIRK-M34,87.2284

and +tonk God of hys grace.  CMMIRK-M34,87.2285

And he +tat ys pore, gruche he noght a+geynes his God, CMMIRK-M34,87.2286

ne deme he not +te rych; CMMIRK-M34,87.2287

but take his pouerte in pacyence CMMIRK-M34,87.2288

and +tonke God of hys grace: CMMIRK-M34,87.2289

for, at +te last, he schall haue +tat for +te best.  CMMIRK-M34,87.2290

But a man, be he ryche or be he pore, yf he haue grace of God, to se
how moche he takyth of God, and how lytyll he +geuyth agayne, verray
reson woll tell +tat he ys more wor+ty dampnacyon +ten saluacyon.
CMMIRK-M34,87.2291

But for God ys full of grace, and schewyth hys grace to all his
hondywerk, and for he knowet oure frelte, he ha+te compassyon of vs,
CMMIRK-M34,87.2292

and +geuyth vs hys grace in abydyng of amendement.  +Tat ys +ta+g thow

CMMIRK-M34,87.2293

for he ha+te moche leuer forto do grace then vengeans.  CMMIRK-M34,87.2294

And +tat ys for two caues, as Saynt Austyne seyth.  CMMIRK-M34,87.2295

On ys, yf God had don vengeans, anon the world had ben endyd mony a day

CMMIRK-M34,87.2296

That o+ter cause ys, forto schewe how full he ys of grace, and how fayn

For, as Saynt Anselm sayth, +te lest synne +tat a man doth, hyt

CMMIRK-M34,88.2306

bot hyth you forto clanse you +terof.  CMMIRK-M34,88.2307

amende hom; CMMIRK-M34,88.2308

and when he smytyth, he smytyth sore.  CMMIRK-M34,88.2309

Narracio.  CMMIRK-M34,88.2311

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, +tys day ys +te secunde Sonday yn clene Lenton.
Wherfor, as +ge haue ben bysy all +tys +gere forto make you clene and

22.  CMMIRK-M34,96.2572

DE DOMINICA TERCIA QUADRAGESIME SERMO BREUIS.  CMMIRK-M34,96.2573

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, +tys ys +te +trydde Sonenday of Lenton.  Wherfor we
redyn yn +te gospell of +tys day how our Lord Ihesu Crist cast out a
dombe fende of a man; CMMIRK-M34,96.2575

+toghtys +tat a man wyth delyte occupyeth his hert yn.  CMMIRK-M34,96.2577

And when he comyth to schryft, +ten ys he dombe, CMMIRK-M34,96.2578

+toght, ne forto speke ydull wordys to make men to lagh, ne forto swer
an oth do+te no harme.  CMMIRK-M34,96.2579

+Gus, for so+te, hit ys such a synne, as Crist sayth hymselfe, +tat a man
schall +geue acownte +terof, yn +te day of dome, of yche ydull word +tat
a man spekyth.  Wherfore forto wythdraw all men of such o+tes and wordys,
Seynt Poule yn +te pystull of +tys day forbedyth yche cristen man not to
speke all maner ydull speche, and rybaudy, and harlatry, and all othyr
speches +tat turnyth to foly and to noght.  And byddyth hom speke suche
wordys +tat ben worschypfull to God, and profet to hom +tat heryn hom.
And byddy+te +tat suche foly wordys and rybawdy schuld not be nempnyd
among Godis pepull; CMMIRK-M34,96.2580

for $+ter $as {TEXT:+teras} +tay ben oft ynempnet, +tay ben +toght on,
CMMIRK-M34,96.2581

and so +tay fallyn ynto +te dede of synne, CMMIRK-M34,96.2582

and +togh +te dede of synne sewe not, neuer+teles +te lyst +tat a man

23.  CMMIRK-M34,101.2720

DE DOMINICA QUARTA QUADRAGESIME.  CMMIRK-M34,101.2721

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, as +ge all know well, +tys ys +te four+te Sonday
of Lenton.  Yn +te wheche day all holy chyrch maky+te mynde of a holy

Crist mony +geres er he was borne of our lady.  CMMIRK-M34,101.2723

24.  CMMIRK-M34,106.2870

DE ANUNCIACIONE DOMINICA SERMO BREUIS.  CMMIRK-M34,106.2871

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, +tat louen to serue our lady, suche a day +ge schull
haue an hegh fest in holy chyrch, +tat ys callyd +te Annunciacyon of
our lady.  +Te whech euen +ge schull fast, ych man aftyr hys deuocyon
, and aftyr he ha+te made a vow, and also as he ys joynet of +te holy
gostly fadyr.  CMMIRK-M34,106.2873

The schull +ge know well +tat +tis fest ys callet +te Annuncyacyon of

For +tys skyll +te hygh Fadyr of Heuen send hys holy angell Gabryell

+tat was called Ioseph.  CMMIRK-M34,106.2875

CMMIRK-M34,106.2876

and sayde:'Heyl be +tou, full of grace; CMMIRK-M34,106.2878

God ys wyth +te; CMMIRK-M34,106.2879

Then was scho gretly abaschot of +tys metyng.  CMMIRK-M34,106.2881

wycchecraft, CMMIRK-M34,106.2882

'CMMIRK-M34,107.2901

+Tus scho conceyued our Lord Ihesu Crist in euerlastyng joy to all
+te world.  CMMIRK-M34,107.2902

CMMIRK-M34,107.2912

25.  CMMIRK-M34,110.3010

DE DOMINICA IN PASSIONE DOMINI NOSTRI IHESU CRISTI.  CMMIRK-M34,110.3011

<$$heading>

Good men and woymen, +tys day ys called yn holy chyrch +te Sonenday yn
+te Passyon; for bycause +tat our Lord Ihesu Cryst began hys passyon
+tys day.  CMMIRK-M34,110.3013

The Iewys and +te Pharyses haden suche envy to hym, for bycause +tat he

wer fully assentyd to do hym to deth.  CMMIRK-M34,110.3014

Oft befor +tay werne about to haue slayne hym, CMMIRK-M34,110.3015

but euer +tay were lettyd by drede of +te pepull; CMMIRK-M34,110.3016

for +te pepull heldyn hym a profyt.  CMMIRK-M34,110.3017

and all forto tempte hym, forto haue made hym to haue spoken summe worde
by +te wheche +tay myght haue put hym to repreue.  CMMIRK-M34,111.3018

haue stenet hym to +te deth; CMMIRK-M34,111.3019

but for he knew well hor malyce, he hudde hym, CMMIRK-M34,111.3020

and +gode from hom out of +te tempull.  CMMIRK-M34,111.3021

and soo +ge haue taght all +tys lond.  Wherfor +tou schalt haue thyn
owne dome. 'CMMIRK-M34,114.3112

Then anon, yn sight of all the pepull, the erth opened CMMIRK-M34,114.3113

and +te justyce fell don ynto hell.  CMMIRK-M34,114.3114

And soo aftyr +te pepull was gretly agast CMMIRK-M34,114.3115

and amendyd hom of hor o+tys.  Wherfor, syrs and dames, do +ge as crysten
men schulden do: CMMIRK-M34,114.3116

leue+t your o+tys, CMMIRK-M34,114.3117

and do+te reuerence to Cristys passyon and to hys wondys,
CMMIRK-M34,114.3118

and techi+te all o+tyr to do +te same.  CMMIRK-M34,114.3119
